    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 48.6 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.54 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.02 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 62.5 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 83.3% of the total average of 75.0 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 28.5 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.01 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                        1
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         0,97
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 16.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 56.6% of the total average of 28.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 1.0 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          1.0 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Threads are executed in groups of 32 threads called warps. This kernel launch is configured to execute 1      
          threads per block. Consequently, some threads in a warp are masked off and those hardware resources are       
          unused. Try changing the number of threads per block to be a multiple of 32 threads. Between 128 and 256      
          threads per block is a good initial range for experimentation. Use smaller thread blocks rather than one      
          large thread block per multiprocessor if latency affects performance. This is particularly beneficial to      
          kernels that frequently call __syncthreads().                                                                 
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   The grid for this launch is configured to execute only 1 blocks, which is less than the GPU's 14              
          multiprocessors. This can underutilize some multiprocessors. If you do not intend to execute this kernel      
          concurrently with other workloads, consider reducing the block size to have at least one block per            
          multiprocessor or increase the size of the grid to fully utilize the available hardware resources.

          issues an instruction every 31.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.90 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

          (IMC) miss. This represents about 50.5% of the total average of 58.9 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 16.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.91 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.07 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 13.0 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 40.7% of the total average of 31.9 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.                                                                                  
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 29.3 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 23.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 33.8 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.72 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

          (IMC) miss. This represents about 51.1% of the total average of 58.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 16.1 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.94 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.07 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 13.3 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 42.4% of the total average of 31.3 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.

    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,06
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 19.2 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.96 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 23.2 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 61.5% of the total average of 37.7 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 23.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.87 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.05 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 26.9 cycles being stalled waiting for sibling warps at a CTA       
          barrier. This represents about 60.9% of the total average of 44.2 cycles between issuing two instructions. A  
          high number of warps waiting at a barrier is commonly caused by diverging code paths before a barrier that    
          causes some warps to wait a long time until other warps reach the synchronization point. Whenever possible    
          try to divide up the work into blocks of uniform workloads. Use the Source View's sampling columns to         
          identify which barrier instruction causes the most stalls and optimize the code executed before that          
          synchronization point first.

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 9.2 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          2.58 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.12 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------

    Section: Scheduler Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           7,25
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,07
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          92,75
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,82
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,09
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 13.8 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.82 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.09 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 17.6 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 70.1% of the total average of 25.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.

    Section: Scheduler Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    Instructions Per Active Issue Slot                                          inst/cycle                              1
    One or More Eligible                                                                 %                           2,65
    Issued Warp Per Scheduler                                                                                        0,03
    No Eligible                                                                          %                          97,35
    Theoretical Warps Per Scheduler                                                   warp                              8
    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,95
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,03
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 37.8 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.95 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.03 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,03
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                       32
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                           32
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 58.8 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 80.1% of the total average of 73.5 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          

    Section: Instruction Statistics
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           3,19
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,06
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 18.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          3.19 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.06 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,06
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    20,80
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        20,46
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 43.9 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 76.3% of the total average of 57.5 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 20.8 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 20.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().
